2. Product Philosophy & Design Principles
2.1 The Dual-Mode Paradigm
The foundational design decision of Kisan Connect is the "One App, Two Modes" architecture. Rather than building four separate apps with four separate user acquisition funnels, the platform presents a single entry point. Upon first registration, users select a Primary Mode. However, the system is engineered to allow any user to hold both a Buyer Profile and a Seller Profile simultaneously, switchable from a persistent toggle in the top navigation bar.
Design Rationale
A farmer who sells crops is also likely to rent equipment and hire labor. A service provider is also a job seeker. Forcing users into single-role apps contradicts the reality of rural economic behavior. The dual-mode approach recognizes and serves this reality, increasing engagement depth and platform lifetime value per user.
2.2 The Eight Design Laws
Every design decision — from screen layout to API response structure — must pass through these eight laws:
Law 1: Connectivity Agnosticism: The app must function fully on zero connectivity. Network is a bonus, not a requirement. Every feature must have an offline fallback.
Law 2: Literacy Inclusivity: The platform must be usable by a person who cannot read. Voice input, icon-first navigation, and audio feedback are not enhancements — they are baseline requirements.
Law 3: Trust by Default: Every transaction carries escrow protection. Every user profile shows verification status. Every review is from a verified transaction. Trust is not earned over time on this platform — it is structurally enforced from day one.
Law 4: Financial Inclusion: Zero minimum transaction value. UPI as the primary payment rail. No credit card required anywhere. Support for feature phone users via USSD fallback.
Law 5: Data Sovereignty: User data belongs to the user. Data is stored encrypted at rest and in transit. PDPB (India Personal Data Protection Bill) compliance is non-negotiable from day one, not retrofitted.
Law 6: Performance Parity: A user on a 2-year-old ₹5,000 Android device must have an experience comparable to a user on a flagship. APK size < 20MB. Initial load < 2 seconds on 3G. Every list screen must render first 10 items in < 500ms.
Law 7: Extreme Localization: Not just translation. Localization includes date formats, weight units (maund, quintal vs kg), currency display, cultural imagery, and local festival calendars in the AI price model.
Law 8: Reversible Architecture: Every decision must be reversible without a full rewrite. Microservices are isolated. Databases are per-service. Payment gateways are swapped behind an abstraction layer. This protects the billion-dollar codebase from vendor lock-in.
3. System Architecture
3.1 Architectural Overview
Kisan Connect is built on a microservices architecture orchestrated behind an API Gateway. Each bounded domain (User Management, each Marketplace, Payments, Notifications, AI/ML) is an independently deployable service with its own private database. Services communicate via asynchronous event queues (Kafka/RabbitMQ) for non-blocking operations and synchronous REST/gRPC calls for real-time queries.

3.2 Microservice Boundaries & Responsibilities
3.2.1 API Gateway
The API Gateway is the single ingress point for all client traffic. It handles:
JWT validation and token refresh before forwarding requests to downstream services
Rate limiting per user per endpoint (configurable per plan tier)
Request/response transformation for versioned APIs
SSL termination and DDoS protection via Cloudflare
Logging of every request with correlation IDs for distributed tracing
A/B testing header injection for experiment routing
3.2.2 User Management Service
Owns the users, user_locations, seller_profiles, buyer_profiles, and verification_documents tables
Issues signed JWTs (RS256) with role claims (buyer, seller, admin, support)
Handles OTP-based phone number authentication via SMS (primary) and WhatsApp (fallback)
Manages KYC document upload, storage, and status tracking
Exposes a gRPC endpoint for other services to validate tokens without round-tripping to the gateway
3.2.3 Marketplace Services (Crop / Equipment / Services / Jobs)
Each service owns its own PostgreSQL schema on Supabase
Communicates with User Service via gRPC for seller/buyer profile lookups
Publishes domain events (ListingCreated, OrderPlaced, BookingConfirmed) to the Kafka event bus
Maintains its own search index via webhook pushes to the Search Service on create/update/delete
Implements pagination using cursor-based pagination (not offset) for consistent results on real-time data
3.2.4 Unified Payment & Financial Services Cluster
The payment cluster is the most critical system and is designed for maximum fault tolerance. It consists of four independent services:
Payment Gateway Service: An abstraction layer over Razorpay (primary) and PhonePe (UPI-specific). Exposes a unified POST /v1/payments/initiate endpoint. Normalizes callback payloads across gateways. Enables hot-swapping of gateways without code changes in upstream services.
Transaction Service: Maintains an immutable append-only ledger of every payment event. Never deletes or updates records — only inserts new state events. Provides the canonical source of truth for payment status.
Escrow Service: Implements a formal state machine (see Section 7.5). Holds funds in a designated bank escrow account. Manages dispute windows, arbitration escalation, and automated releases.
Commission & Ledger Service: Calculates and records commission splits in real time when escrow releases. Manages seller payout schedules (daily/weekly). Maintains separate ledger accounts for the platform, each seller wallet, and the refund reserve.
3.3 Event-Driven Communication
All cross-service communication that does not require an immediate synchronous response is handled via the Kafka event bus. This ensures services are loosely coupled and the system remains operational even if a downstream service is temporarily unavailable.
